## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the central problem in population dynamics. The relationship between growth rate and population size reveals the underlying ecological mechanisms (density dependence, carrying capacity, Allee effects, etc.).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth common in tumor/population modeling)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 + P) (reduced per-capita growth at low density)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible asymmetric growth curve)
- Time-varying exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (growth rate changing with time)
- Logistic with time-varying rate: dP_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * P * (1 - c2 * P) (seasonally or temporally modulated logistic)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (allometric scaling of growth rate)
- Harvesting/mortality logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (logistic growth with proportional harvesting)
- Cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial approximation of complex density effects)
- Oscillatory forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal environmental forcing on logistic growth)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear dependence of dP/dt on P → exponential (Malthusian) growth regime; look for dP_dt proportional to P
- Quadratic dependence (P and P²) → logistic-type density dependence with carrying capacity
- Cubic terms in P → Allee effect or bistability with multiple equilibria
- dP/dt = 0 at specific nonzero P values → carrying capacity or extinction thresholds as fixed points
- Logarithmic terms log(P) → Gompertz-type growth with multiplicative rather than additive density regulation
- Fractional power P**c with 0<c<1 → surface-area-limited growth (e.g., nutrient absorption through membranes)
- Explicit time dependence in growth rate → non-autonomous dynamics, environmental change, or seasonal effects
- Product of multiple factors involving P → multiple ecological mechanisms acting simultaneously (e.g., Allee + carrying capacity)
- Ratio of polynomials in P → Holling-type functional responses or resource-limited per-capita growth rates
- Growth rate that changes sign at specific P values → bifurcation structure revealing stable/unstable equilibria

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and determine if any candidate can match it.

**GT Analysis:**

The GT is:
```
0.201*(-1 + P/5.637)*(1 - P/10.233)*P + 0.201*P + 0.201*P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(-0.634 + P)))
```

Let me expand the first term:
(-1 + P/5.637)(1 - P/10.233) = -1 + P/10.233 + P/5.637 - P²/(5.637×10.233)

So the first part times 0.201*P:
= 0.201*P*(-1 + P/10.233 + P/5.637 - P²/57.68)
= -0.201P + 0.201P²/10.233 + 0.201P²/5.637 - 0.201P³/57.68

Combined with +0.201P, the -0.201P cancels:
= 0.201P²(1/10.233 + 1/5.637) - 0.201P³/57.68 + 0.201P/(1 + exp(-5.637(-0.634 + P)))

So GT = c₀*P³ + c₁*P² + sigmoid_term

The sigmoid term is: 0.201*P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(P - 0.634)))

Note that P/(1 + exp(-a(P-b))) can be related to softplus or logistic functions.

Key observation: The sigmoid σ(x) = 1/(1+exp(-x)), so the term is 0.201*P*σ(5.637*(P-0.634)).

Now, tanh and sigmoid are related: σ(x) = (1 + tanh(x/2))/2, so:
P*σ(a(P-b)) = P*(1 + tanh(a(P-b)/2))/2 = P/2 + P*tanh(a(P-b)/2)/2

So GT = c₀P³ + c₁P² + 0.201*(P/2 + P*tanh(5.637*(P-0.634)/2)/2)
= c₀P³ + c₁P² + 0.1005P + 0.1005*P*tanh(2.818*(P - 0.634))
= c₀P³ + c₁P² + 0.1005P + 0.1005*P*tanh(2.818P - 1.787)

So the GT has the form: P³*a + P²*b + P*c + P*d*tanh(eP + f)

Now checking candidates:

**Candidate 5**: `P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + Pc3*tanh(Pc4 + c5) + c6*log(c7*exp(Pc8) + 1)`

The log(c7*exp(Pc8)+1) term - if c6=0, this reduces to P³c0+P²c1+Pc2+Pc3*tanh(Pc4+c5), which matches the form. But we need to check if we need that log term. Setting c6=0 works.

**Candidate 8**: `P³c0 + P²c1 + P²c2 + Pc3 + Pc4*tanh(Pc5 + c6) + Pc7`
= P³c0 + P²(c1+c2) + P(c3+c7) + Pc4*tanh(Pc5+c6)
This has the form P³a + P²b + Pc + Pd*tanh(eP+f). ✓

**Candidate 29**: `P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2*tanh(Pc3 + c4) + P`
This is P³c0 + P²c1 + P + Pc2*tanh(Pc3+c4). The linear P term is fixed at 1, but GT needs ~0.1005. No free constant to adjust. ✗

**Candidate 5** with c6=0: P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + Pc3*tanh(Pc4+c5). This matches! ✓

**Candidate 8** also matches. ✓

**Candidate 35**: `P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + Pc3*tanh(P+c4) + Pc5`
Here tanh argument is P+c4, not Pc4+c5 - we can't scale P inside tanh. The GT needs tanh(2.818P - 1.787), but this only allows tanh(P + c4). Not equivalent unless the coefficient is exactly 1. ✗

**Candidate 5** works (setting c6=0).
**Candidate 8** works.

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) and compare each candidate to it.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
```
0.201*(-1 + P/5.637)*(1 - P/10.233)*P + 0.201*P + 0.201*P/(1 + exp(-5.637*(-0.634 + P)))
```

Let me expand the first term:
- (-1 + P/5.637)(1 - P/10.233) = -1 + P/10.233 + P/5.637 - P²/(5.637×10.233)
- = -1 + P(1/10.233 + 1/5.637) - P²/57.68

Multiplying by P:
- = -P + P²(1/10.233 + 1/5.637) - P³/57.68

Multiplying by 0.201:
- = -0.201P + 0.201P²(0.0977 + 0.1774) - 0.201P³/57.68
- = -0.201P + 0.201×0.2751×P² - 0.00348P³
- = -0.201P + 0.0553P² - 0.00348P³

Adding 0.201P: the linear terms cancel, giving:
**GT ≈ -0.00348P³ + 0.0553P² + 0.201P/(1 + exp(-5.637(P - 0.634)))**

So the GT has the structure: **cubic P³ + quadratic P² + sigmoid-like term involving P**.

The sigmoid term `P/(1 + exp(-5.637(P-0.634)))` is a P times a logistic function of P.

Key structural features:
1. P³ term
2. P² term  
3. A nonlinear sigmoid/logistic-type term in P
4. **No dependence on t**
5. No constant term (everything multiplied by P)

Now let me check which candidates can match. Any candidate with `t` dependence that can't be zeroed out is eliminated. The sigmoid term needs to be matched by something equivalent.

**Important:** `P/(1+exp(-a(P-b)))` can be written using:
- `tanh`: since sigmoid(x) = (1+tanh(x/2))/2, so P/(1+exp(-x)) = P·sigmoid(x) = P(1+tanh(x/2))/2
- `log(exp(...)+1)`: since log(exp(x)+1) = x·sigmoid(x) + log(1+exp(-x))... not straightforward

Let me verify: `P*tanh(aP+b)` form.
sigmoid(x) = (1+tanh(x/2))/2, so P·sigmoid(5.637(P-0.634)) = P(1+tanh(5.637(P-0.634)/2))/2 = P/2 + P·tanh(2.818P - 1.787)/2

So the sigmoid term 0.201·P·sigmoid(5.637(P-0.634)) = 0.201P/2 + 0.201P·tanh(2.818P-1.787)/2 = 0.1005P + 0.1005P·tanh(2.818P-1.787)

So GT = -0.00348P³ + 0.0553P² + 0.1005P + 0.1005P·tanh(2.818P - 1.787)

This means GT = **c0·P³ + c1·P² + c2·P + c3·P·tanh(c4·P + c5)**

Now let me also check `log(c·exp(aP)+1)`:
log(exp(x)+1) = softplus(x). Note that P·sigmoid(x) ≠ softplus(x) in general. So `P*sigmoid` ≠ `log(exp+1)`.

Actually, let me reconsider Candidate 5: `P*c3*tanh(P*c4+c5) + c6*log(c7*exp(P*c8)+1)`. This has both tanh AND log terms - could potentially work but would need exact cancellation.

Let me now systematically check candidates that have the right structure: **P³ + P² + P·tanh(aP+b) + P** (no t dependence, no constant term).

### Candidates with tanh and no t:

**Candidate 5:** `P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + Pc3·tanh(Pc4+c5) + c6·log(c7·exp(Pc8)+1)`
The log term: log(c7·exp(Pc8)+1). If c7=1, this is softplus(Pc8). This adds an extra basis function that can't be zeroed without losing it. Setting c6=0 removes it, giving P³+P²+P+P·tanh, which matches the structure. Yes, this works!

Wait, but we need to check if the log term could contribute. Setting c6=0 gives exactly the right structure.

Candidate 5 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 7:** `P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + Pc3·tanh(P+c4) + c5·exp(P²c6)`
tanh(P+c4) vs tanh(c4·P+c5) - here the coefficient of P inside tanh is fixed at 1, but GT needs ~2.818. Can't match.

Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 8:** `P³c0 + P²c1 + P²c2 + Pc3 + Pc4·tanh(Pc5+c6) + Pc7`
= P³c0 + P²(c1+c2) + P(c3+c7) + Pc4·tanh(Pc5+c6). This is P³+P²+P+P·tanh(aP+b). Matches!

Candidate 8 verdict: [MATCH]

Set c7=0 (or c5=0). If c5=0: same as 29, P coefficient fixed at 1. If c7=0: P³c0+P²c1+Pc2·tanh(Pc3+c4)+P+c5·exp(Pc6). The exp(Pc6) is a different basis function. Can't match.

Candidate 34 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 35:** `P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + Pc3·tanh(P+c4) + Pc5`
tanh(P+c4): coefficient of P inside tanh is 1, need ~2.818. No match.

Candidate 35 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 38:** `P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + Pc3·tanh(P+c4)`
Same issue - tanh(P+c4) has fixed coefficient 1 on P.

Candidate 38 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 39:** `P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2·tanh(Pc3+c4)`
Missing the linear P term. tanh ranges from -1 to 1, so Pc2·tanh can't provide a constant linear component plus the tanh variation simultaneously. Actually, tanh(Pc3+c4) approaches ±1 for large |P|, so asymptotically this gives ±c2·P, but the GT has both a linear term and a tanh term. With only one tanh term and no separate linear P, we can't match both.

Wait - actually we can decompose: c2·P·tanh(c3P+c4) already contains both linear-like and nonlinear behavior. But the GT is c_a·P + c_b·P·tanh(c_c·P+c_d). These are two independent functions (P and P·tanh(aP+b)) and can't be combined into a single P·tanh term.

Candidate 39 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 48:** `P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2·tanh(P+c3)`
Same issues as 39 plus fixed tanh coefficient.

Candidate 48 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 50:** `P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + Pc3·tanh(Pc4+c5) + c6·log(c7t+1)`
Set c6=0 to remove t. Then: P³c0+P²c1+Pc2+Pc3·tanh(Pc4+c5). This matches!

Candidate 50 verdict: [MATCH]

Now let me check candidates with `exp(P·c)` terms that might replicate the sigmoid:

**Candidate 49:** `P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + Pc3·exp(Pc4)`
P·exp(aP) is not equivalent to P·sigmoid(aP). No match.

Candidate 49 verdict: [NO MATCH]

Missing P term, has exp and constant. exp(aP) ≠ P·sigmoid. No match.
